The most significant friction points between current findings and established theory are:
1. The "Impossible" Early Galaxies

JWST has identified galaxies like MoM-z14, observed as they appeared only 280 million years after the Big Bang.

    The Problem: These galaxies are not just present; they are massive, bright, and chemically "mature" (containing heavy elements like nitrogen).

    Logical Conflict: Under the standard model, it should take billions of years for stars to live, die, and seed the universe with these metals. Finding them 280 million years in suggests either the universe is much older than 13.8 billion years, or the rate of star formation in the early universe was orders of magnitude faster than physics currently allows.

2. The Hubble Tension Confirmation

Multiple studies in early 2026 have used JWST to cross-check Hubble's measurements of the expansion rate of the universe (H0​).

    The Finding: JWST has confirmed that the universe is expanding approximately 8% faster than the "afterglow" of the Big Bang (the Cosmic Microwave Background) predicts.

    Impact: This eliminates "human error" or "instrumental bias" as explanations. There is a fundamental "tension" in the fabric of reality—the universe we see today doesn't match the math of the universe we started with.

3. "Little Red Dots" and "Dark Stars"

JWST is spotting compact, extremely red objects in the deep past.

    Fact: Many of these have been identified as young supermassive black holes "feeding" inside dense cocoons of gas.

    [Inference]: Some researchers are proposing these could be Dark Stars—massive objects powered by dark matter annihilation rather than nuclear fusion. If Dark Stars exist, they would provide a "missing link" for how supermassive black holes formed so quickly without needing traditional star lifecycles.

4. Asymmetry of the Universe

[Pattern]: Recent analysis suggests the universe may be asymmetrical or "lopsided," meaning it does not look the same in all directions.
